Lenstool pipeline using systems 1 and 2 as constraints as well as two other systems with spectroscopic redshift measurements.\n<a name=\"apjab929dt4fnb\" id=\"apjab929dt4fnb\"></a><sup> b</sup>Standard deviation of the magnification values between the different models.\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/898/1/6/suppdata/apjab929dt4_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/ab929d\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/898/1/6/1/apjab929dt4_lr.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1637170761&amp;Signature=JWYXVVdNc3AYbzJrOoMygm2Ua50%3D\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>Here, we compare in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjab929dt4\">4</a> the magnification estimated for each image of the system derived by the LTM, dPIEeNFW, Lenstool, and GLAFIC algorithms and the model presented in Dessauges-Zavadsky et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab929dbib19\" id=\"fnref-apjab929dbib19\">2017</a>). The magnification values between the strong-lens models differ significantly (the dispersion between models being larger than the statistical uncertainties), which makes a reliable estimation of the intrinsic properties of the background source challenging. It will be interesting, when more spectroscopic data becomes available, to analyze if the lens models converge toward similar magnification values.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjab929ds7\" name=\"apjab929ds7\">7.\u00a0Summary</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>The RELICS survey was designed to efficiently discover and characterize bright high-redshift galaxies that are magnified by massive cluster lenses, as well as to identify which galaxy clusters are the most efficient lenses for future follow-up campaigns (Coe et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab929dbib17\" id=\"fnref-apjab929dbib17\">2019</a>). Based mostly on RELICS observations, we present here a full SL analysis of the merging galaxy cluster RXC J0032.1+1808. More recently, efforts have focused on SL systematic uncertainties arising from different modeling techniques (Johnson &amp; Sharon <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab929dbib32\" id=\"fnref-apjab929dbib32\">2016</a>; Meneghetti et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab929dbib43\" id=\"fnref-apjab929dbib43\">2017</a>; Remolina Gonz\u00e1lez et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab929dbib56\" id=\"fnref-apjab929dbib56\">2018</a>). In this work, we have adopted two different methodologies, the LTM technique and a fully parametric model, dPIEeNFW. We have also compared our results with the models obtained with the Lenstool and GLAFIC pipelines, that were independently constructed, so that our conclusions can be made more robust. As we show throughout, the results for most quantities of interest seem to agree fairly well between the different models. In that sense, differences between the LTM, dPIEeNFW, Lenstool and GLAFIC resulting models are then more representative of the true underlying uncertainties than the magnitude of the statistical uncertainties from the respective minimization procedures.</p><p>The derived mass distribution and Einstein radius of RXC0032 reveals a very prominent lens, with a large effective Einstein radius of <em>\u03b8</em><sub>E</sub>\u00a0\u223c\u00a040'' at <em>z</em><sub><em>s</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.0, as supported by all models probed here. Since mergers enhance the lensing cross section, merging clusters such as RXC0032 are of particular interest for the statistical study of the strongest gravitational lenses and are particularly useful when comparing Einstein radius distributions from observations to those from theoretical expectations (Redlich et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab929dbib54\" id=\"fnref-apjab929dbib54\">2012</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab929dbib55\" id=\"fnref-apjab929dbib55\">2014</a>). While RELICS has only uncovered three high-redshift galaxy candidates in this field (Salmon et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab929dbib61\" id=\"fnref-apjab929dbib61\">2020</a>), we find that RXC0032 is a promising lens to carry out wider and deeper imaging follow-up in order to expand the present coverage to all high-magnification regions.</p><p>All the lens models presented in this work and their corresponding deflection fields, magnification maps for different redshifts, as well as 100 random models to calculate errors, are made publicly available through the MAST archive<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjab929dfn3\">27</a></sup>.</p></div>\n<div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We kindly thank the anonymous referee for the insightful and useful comments. This work is based on observations taken by the RELICS Treasury Program (GO-14096) with the NASA/ESA HST. Program GO-14096 is supported by NASA through a grant from the Space Telescope Science Institute, which is operated by the Association of Universities for Research in Astronomy, Inc., under NASA contract NAS5-26555. This work was performed in part under the auspices of the U.S. Department of Energy by Lawrence Livermore National Laboratory under Contract DE-AC52-07NA27344. This work was supported in part by World Premier International Research Center Initiative (WPI Initiative), MEXT, Japan, and JSPS KAKENHI grant Nos. JP15H05892 and JP18K03693. K.U. acknowledges support from the Ministry of Science and Technology of Taiwan under the grant MOST 106-2628-M-001-003-MY3. This work is partially supported by the Australian Research Council Centre of Excellence for All-Sky Astrophysics in 3 Dimensions (ASTRO-3D). S.T. acknowledges support from the ERC Consolidator Grant funding scheme (project ConTExt, grant No. 648179). The Cosmic Dawn Center is funded by the Danish National Research Foundation.</p><p><em>Facilities:</em> HST - Hubble Space Telescope satellite,  Spitzer - ,  MAST. - \n</p></div><h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjab929dapp1\" name=\"apjab929dapp1\">Appendix A: List of Multiple Images and Candidate Identifications for RXC J0032.1+1808</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We present in Tables <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjab929dt5\">A1</a> and <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjab929dt6\">A2</a> the list of multiple images used in this work, as well as candidate identifications. uncovered. Those identified with a \"c\" refer to less reliable therefore candidate identifications that were not included in our SL models. Systems identified with an \"L\" or \"G\" refer to those independently identified by the Lenstool and GLAFIC modeling teams, respectively.\n<a name=\"apjab929dt5fnb\" id=\"apjab929dt5fnb\"></a><sup> b</sup>Photometric redshift with upper and lower limits, based on the BPZ estimates from the RELICS catalog with the 95% confidence range; a \"-\" sign indicates an image for which its <em>z</em><sub>phot</sub> could not be measured due to light contamination or poor signal-to-noise ratio.\n<a name=\"apjab929dt5fnc\" id=\"apjab929dt5fnc\"></a><sup> c</sup>Redshift prediction based on our LTM and analytical dPIEeNFW best-fit models, respectively.\n<a name=\"apjab929dt5fnd\" id=\"apjab929dt5fnd\"></a><sup> d</sup>The symbol \u2713 indicates whether a multiple image is used in the SL modeling by the LTM/dPIEeNFW, Lenstool and GLAFIC pipelines.\n<a name=\"apjab929dt5fne\" id=\"apjab929dt5fne\"></a><sup> e</sup>Rms between the observed and model-predicted multiple images from our LTM best-fit model.\n<a name=\"apjab929dt5fnf\" id=\"apjab929dt5fnf\"></a><sup> f</sup>Measured by Dessauges-Zavadsky et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab929dbib19\" id=\"fnref-apjab929dbib19\">2017</a>), considered as a fixed redshift in our SL models.\n<a name=\"apjab929dt5fng\" id=\"apjab929dt5fng\"></a><sup> g</sup>We fix the redshift of system 7 which is a \"dropout\" object.\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table J0032.1+1808</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We present here the reproduction of the multiple images identified in RXC J0032.1+1808's field with our LTM pipeline (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab929df6\">B1</a>), as well as HST cutouts for the additional images independently identified by the Lenstool and GLAFIC lensing teams
